# Task: Generate Operational Runbook for Prometheus TSDB Compaction

**Repository:** prometheus/prometheus
**Output:** Write your runbook to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an operational runbook for Prometheus's TSDB (Time Series Database) compaction process. TSDB compaction merges overlapping time blocks, removes tombstoned series, and maintains query performance over time.

## Scope

Explore the TSDB compaction implementation in:
- `tsdb/compact.go` — core compaction logic
- `tsdb/head_read.go` and `tsdb/head.go` — head block behavior
- `tsdb/db.go` — database lifecycle and compaction triggering

## Required Sections

Your runbook at `/workspace/documentation.md` must include:

### 1. Overview
- What compaction does and why it is needed
- Compaction levels and block structure
- When compaction is triggered (time-based, size-based)

### 2. Monitoring Indicators
- Key Prometheus metrics to watch during compaction (e.g., `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total`, `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds`)
- Alert thresholds and what they indicate
- How to distinguish healthy vs. stuck compaction

### 3. Failure Modes
- At least 4 failure modes with symptoms and causes:
  - Disk space exhaustion
  - Compaction stuck / not progressing
  - Block corruption
  - OOM during compaction
- For each: symptom, likely cause, and diagnostic steps

### 4. Recovery Procedures
- Step-by-step recovery for each failure mode
- When to restart Prometheus vs. manual block manipulation
- How to use `promtool tsdb` commands for inspection/repair

### 5. Code Reference
- Key functions in the codebase relevant to each failure mode

## Quality Bar

- Metric names must be real (verify in the codebase)
- Recovery steps must be numbered and actionable
- Each failure mode must link to a specific code location

   355→// splitByRange splits the directories by the time range. The range sequence starts at 0.
   356→//
   357→// For example, if we have blocks [0-10, 10-20, 50-60, 90-100] and the split range tr is 30
   358→// it returns [0-10, 10-20], [50-60], [90-100].
   359→func splitByRange(ds []dirMeta, tr int64) [][]dirMeta {
   360→	var splitDirs [][]dirMeta
   361→
   362→	for i := 0; i < len(ds); {
   363→		var (
   364→			group []dirMeta
   365→			t0    int64
   366→			m     = ds[i].meta
   367→		)
   368→		// Compute start of aligned time range of size tr closest to the current block's start.
   369→		if m.MinTime >= 0 {
   370→			t0 = tr * (m.MinTime / tr)
   371→		} else {
   372→			t0 = tr * ((m.MinTime - tr + 1) / tr)
   373→		}
   374→		// Skip blocks that don't fall into the range. This can happen via mis-alignment or
   375→		// by being the multiple of the intended range.
   376→		if m.MaxTime > t0+tr {
   377→			i++
   378→			continue
   379→		}
   380→
   381→		// Add all dirs to the current group that are within [t0, t0+tr].
   382→		for ; i < len(ds); i++ {
   383→			// Either the block falls into the next range or doesn't fit at all (checked above).
   384→			if ds[i].meta.MaxTime > t0+tr {
   385→				break
   386→			}
   387→			group = append(group, ds[i])
   388→		}
   389→
   390→		if len(group) > 0 {
   391→			splitDirs = append(splitDirs, group)
   392→		}
   393→	}
   394→
   395→	return splitDirs
   396→}

## Comprehensive Overview of Prometheus TSDB Compaction Architecture

Based on my exploration of the Prometheus TSDB codebase (v2.52.0), here's a detailed analysis of the compaction implementation:

---

## 1. Core Compaction Type and Interface

### **Compactor Interface** (`/workspace/tsdb/compact.go`)
The system defines a `Compactor` interface with three main operations:

```go
type Compactor interface {
    Plan(dir string) ([]string, error)
    Write(dest string, b BlockReader, mint, maxt int64, base *BlockMeta) (ulid.ULID, error)
    Compact(dest string, dirs []string, open []*Block) (ulid.ULID, error)
}
```

### **LeveledCompactor Implementation**
The primary implementation is `LeveledCompactor`, which manages multi-level block compaction:

```go
type LeveledCompactor struct {
    metrics                     *CompactorMetrics
    logger                      log.Logger
    ranges                      []int64  // Time ranges for each compaction level
    chunkPool                   chunkenc.Pool
    ctx                         context.Context
    maxBlockChunkSegmentSize    int64
    mergeFunc                   storage.VerticalChunkSeriesMergeFunc
    postingsEncoder             index.PostingsEncoder
    enableOverlappingCompaction bool
}
```

---

- Triggered when the head block becomes "compactable"
- **Condition**: `(MaxTime - MinTime) > (chunkRange / 2) * 3` (i.e., 1.5× the chunk range)
- Default chunk range: **2 hours** (`De

  1357→func (db *DB) compactBlocks() (err error) {
  1358→	// Check for compactions of multiple blocks.
  1359→	for {
  1360→		// If we have a lot of blocks to compact the whole process might take
  1361→		// long enough that we end up with a HEAD block that needs to be written.
  1362→		// Check if that's the case and stop compactions early.
  1363→		if db.head.compactable() {
  1364→			level.Warn(db.logger).Log("msg", "aborting block compactions to persit the head block")
  1365→			return nil
  1366→		}
  1367→
  1368→		plan, err := db.compactor.Plan(db.dir)
  1369→		if err != nil {
  1370→			return fmt.Errorf("plan compaction: %w", err)
  1371→		}
  1372→		if len(plan) == 0 {
  1373→			break
  1374→		}
  1375→
  1376→		select {
  1377→		case <-db.stopc:
  1378→			return nil
  1379→		default:
  1380→		}
  1381→
  1382→		uid, err := db.compactor.Compact(db.dir, plan, db.blocks)
  1383→		if err != nil {
  1384→			return fmt.Errorf("compact %s: %w", plan, err)
  1385→		}
  1386→

  1388→			if err := os.RemoveAll(filepath.Join(db.dir, uid.String())); err != nil {
  1389→				return fmt.Errorf("delete compacted block after failed db reloadBlocks:%s: %w", uid, err)
  1390→			}
  1391→			return fmt.Errorf("reloadBlocks blocks: %w", err)
  1392→		}
  1393→	}
  1394→
  1395→	return nil
  1396→}

843 /workspace/documentation.md
# Prometheus TSDB Compaction Operational Runbook

## 1. Overview

### Purpose of Compaction

TSDB (Time Series Database) compaction in Prometheus serves three critical functions:

1. **Block Consolidation**: Merges overlapping time blocks to reduce the number of files that need to be queried
2. **Tombstone Cleanup**: Physically removes series marked for deletion by applying tombstone metadata, reducing disk footprint
3. **Query Performance**: Maintains optimal query performance by keeping block sizes and levels balanced according to exponential growth

Without compaction, Prometheus would accumulate small blocks indefinitely, degrading query performance and consuming excessive disk space. Compaction is triggered automatically by Prometheus and typically requires no manual intervention.

### Block Structure and Compaction Levels

**Block Basics**:
- Each block represents a time-ordered chunk of time series data
- Blocks have half-open time intervals: `[MinTime, MaxTime)` where MaxTime is exclusive
- Block structure includes: chunks (samples), index (series metadata), tombstones (deletion markers), meta.json (metadata)

## Runbook Contents (843 lines)

### ✅ 1. Overview
- **Purpose**: Block consolidation, tombstone cleanup, query performance maintenance
- **Block structure**: Time intervals, metadata, compaction levels
- **Compaction triggers**: Time-based (3h threshold), periodic checks (1m), on-commit signals
- **Exponential leveling**: Blocks grow exponentially (2h → 6h → 18h → 54h...)

### ✅ 2. Monitoring Indicators
**Real metrics verified from `tsdb/compact.go:100-151`**:
- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` — compaction count
- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block` — stuck detection (gauge 0/1)
- `prometheus_tsdb_vertical_compactions_total` — overlapping block compactions
- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds` — duration histogram
- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_size_bytes`, `chunk_samples`, `chunk_range_seconds`

**Healthy vs. stuck patterns** with exact symptoms and alert thresholds

### ✅ 3. Four Failure Modes with Diagnostic Steps

**Failure Mode 1: Disk Space Exhaustion**
- Symptoms, causes, 7-step recovery (orphaned dirs, retention policies, manual compaction)

**Failure Mode 2: Compaction Stuck/Not Progressing**
- Detection via goroutine dumps, pprof, I/O monitoring
- Recovery: graceful shutdown → restart → verification

**Failure Mode 3: Block Corruption**
- Detection with `promtool analyze`, file verification
- Recovery: backup before deletion, filesystem check with fsck

**Failure Mode 4: Out-of-Memory (OOM)**
- Early detection before OOM kill occurs
- Solutions: add RAM, increase swap, reduce retention

- Each failure mode has numbered, acti

Core Compaction Type and Interface\n\n### **Compactor Interface** (`/workspace/tsdb/compact.go`)\nThe system defines a `Compactor` interface with three main operations:\n\n```go\ntype Compactor interface {\n    Plan(dir string) ([]string, error)\n    Write(dest string, b BlockReader, mint, maxt int64, base *BlockMeta) (ulid.ULID, error)\n    Compact(dest string, dirs []string, open []*Block) (ulid.ULID, error)\n}\n```\n\n### **LeveledCompactor Implementation**\nThe primary implementation is `LeveledCompactor`, which manages multi-level block compaction:\n\n```go\ntype LeveledCompactor struct {\n    metrics                     *CompactorMetrics\n    logger                      log.Logger\n    ranges                      []int64  // Time ranges for each compaction level\n    chunkPool                   chunkenc.Pool\n    ctx                         context.Context\n    maxBlockChunkSegmentSize    int64\n    mergeFunc                   storage.VerticalChunkSeriesMergeFunc\n    postingsEncoder             index.PostingsEncoder\n    enableOverlappingCompaction bool\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Compaction Triggering Mechanisms\n\n### **Time-Based and Size-Based Triggers**\n\nCompaction is triggered through **three main pathways**:\n\n#### a) **Head Block Compaction (Primary)**\n- Triggered when the head block becomes \"compactable\"\n- **Condition**: `(MaxTime - MinTime) > (chunkRange / 2) * 3` (i.e., 1.5\u00d7 the chunk range)\n- Default chunk range: **2 hours** (`DefaultBlockDuration = 2 * time.Hour / time.Millisecond`)\n- This ensures data is compacted after ~3 hours\n\n**From `head.go:1630-1639`:**\n```go\nfunc (h *Head) compactable() bool {\n    if !h.initialized() {\n        return false\n    }\n    return h.MaxTime()-h.MinTime() > h.chunkRange.Load()/2*3\n}\n```\n\n#### b) **Periodic Trigger (1-minute interval)**\nIn `db.go:982-1027`, the DB runs a periodic goroutine that:\n- Reloads blocks every 1 minute\n- Sends a signal to the compaction channel\n- Attempts to memory-map head chunks\n\n#### c) **On-Commit Trigger**\nWhen samples are appended via `dbAppender.Commit()` in `db.go:1115-1127`:\n- Checks if head is compactable\n- Signals compaction channel if needed (non-blocking, buffered with capacity 1)\n\n### **Block Compaction (Leveled)**\nAfter head compaction, the system compacts persisted blocks using:\n- Exponential block ranges (configurable levels)\n- Overlapping block detection and vertical compaction\n\n---\n\n## 3. Compaction Levels and Block Structure\n\n### **Exponential Block Ranges**\n\n```go\nfunc ExponentialBlockRanges(minSize int64, steps, stepSize int) []int64 {\n    ranges := make([]int64, 0, steps)\n    curRange := minSize\n    for i := 0; i < steps; i++ {\n        ranges = append(ranges, curRange)\n        curRange *= int64(stepSize)\n    }\n    return ranges\n}\n```\n\n**Default Configuration** (from `db.go:745-749`):\n- Min block duration: 2 hours\n- Max block duration: 2 hours\n- Ranges created: 10 levels with step size 3\n- Results in: [2h, 6h, 18h, 54h, 162h, 486h, ...] (approximately)\n\n### **BlockMeta Structure** (`/workspace/tsdb/block.go:162-212`)\n\n```go\ntype BlockMeta struct {\n    ULID       ulid.ULID                  // Unique identifier\n    MinTime    int64                      // Block start time (milliseconds)\n    MaxTime    int64                      // Block end time (milliseconds)\n    Stats      BlockStats                 // Counts: samples, series, chunks, tombstones\n    Compaction BlockMetaCompaction        // Compaction history\n    Version    int                        // Index format version\n}\n\ntype BlockMetaCompaction struct {\n    Level       int           // Compaction depth (0=head, 1+=compacted blocks)\n    Sources     []ulid.ULID   // All source head blocks\n    Deletable   bool          // Mark for deletion\n    Parents     []BlockDesc   // Direct parent blocks\n    Failed      bool          // Compaction failure flag\n    Hints       []string      // Metadata: \"from-out-of-order\"\n}\n```\n\n**Block Time Ranges**: Half-open intervals `[MinTime, MaxTime)` where `MaxTime` is exclusive\n\n---\n\n## 4. Main Compaction Steps\n\n### **Step 1: Planning** (`Plan()`)\n**Location**: `compact.go:222-240`\n\n1. Read all block directories\n2. Load metadata for each block\n3. Sort blocks by MinTime\n4. Call internal planning logic:\n   - Check for **overlapping blocks** first (vertical compaction)\n   - If no overlaps, select non-overlapping blocks to compact\n   - Exclude the most recent block (allows backup window)\n   - Compact any block with >5% tombstones (cleanup)\n\n### **Step 2: Selection Logic**\n\n**Overlapping Blocks** (`selectOverlappingDirs`):\n- Detects time range overlaps\n- Returns all overlapping blocks as a group\n- Enabled if `enableOverlappingCompaction = true`\n\n**Non-Overlapping Blocks** (`selectDirs`):\n- Groups blocks into time ranges using `splitByRange()`\n- Selects full ranges that fit exponential buckets\n- Skips ranges containing failed compactions\n- Ignores most recent block (for write window safety)\n\n**Tombstone Cleanup**:\n- Blocks with time range \u2265 50% of midpoint AND >5% tombstones are recompacted\n- All-deleted blocks (tombstones \u2265 series count) are always recompacted\n\n### **Step 3: Compaction** (`Compact()`)\n**Location**: `compact.go:444-537`\n\n1. Open all source blocks (or reuse already-open ones)\n2. Generate new ULID for output block\n3. Merge metadata: `CompactBlockMetas()`\n   - Increment compaction level\n   - Collect all source UIDs\n   - Record parent blocks\n4. Call `write()` to persist merged data\n5. Handle empty result:\n   - Mark source blocks as `Deletable`\n   - Return empty ULID\n   - Log result\n\n### **Step 4: Data Writing** (`write()`)\n**Location**: `compact.go:607-718`\n\n1. Create temporary directory: `{ULID}.tmp-for-creation`\n2. **Populate blocks** (`PopulateBlock`):\n   - Merge chunk series from all input blocks\n   - Apply tombstones (delete marked samples)\n   - Merge and deduplicate series\n   - Write chunks and index\n3. Close chunk and index writers\n4. Write new meta.json with stats\n5. Create empty tombstones file\n6. Sync filesystem\n7. Atomically move `tmp-for-creation` \u2192 final block directory\n\n### **Block Population** (`PopulateBlock`)\n**Location**: `compact.go:729-875`\n\nFor each input block:\n1. Open index, chunks, and tombstones readers\n2. Merge symbols from all blocks\n3. Merge all chunk series sets\n4. For each merged series:\n   - Filter deleted chunks via tombstones\n   - Skip all-deleted series\n   - Write chunks to chunk writer\n   - Write series to index\n   - Update stats (samples, series, chunks counts)\n5. Return merged block\n\n---\n\n## 5. Error Handling\n\n### **Compaction Failure Marking**\n\n**Location**: `compact.go:527-535`\n\nWhen `write()` fails:\n```go\nerrs := tsdb_errors.NewMulti(err)\nif !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n    for _, b := range bs {\n        if err := b.setCompactionFailed(); err != nil {\n            errs.Add(...)\n        }\n    }\n}\nreturn uid, errs.Err()\n```\n\nSets `BlockMetaCompaction.Failed = true` in source blocks' metadata, preventing them from being selected again.\n\n### **Context Cancellation**\n- Compaction respects context cancellation\n- Checks during heavy operations (symbol merge, series iteration)\n- Different error handling for cancellation vs. failures\n\n### **Metrics & Monitoring**\n\n**Location**: `compact.go:89-151`\n\n```go\ntype CompactorMetrics struct {\n    Ran                prometheus.Counter   // Total compactions run\n    PopulatingBlocks   prometheus.Gauge     // Currently writing block\n    OverlappingBlocks  prometheus.Counter   // Vertical compactions count\n    Duration           prometheus.Histogram // Compaction time distribution\n    ChunkSize          prometheus.Histogram // Chunk size on level 1\n    ChunkSamples       prometheus.Histogram // Samples per chunk on level 1\n    ChunkRange         prometheus.Histogram // Time range per chunk on level 1\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Integration with Database Lifecycle\n\n### **From `db.go`**\n\n**Initialization** (lines 830-839):\n```go\ndb.compactor, err = NewLeveledCompactorWithOptions(\n    ctx, r, l, rngs, db.chunkPool,\n    LeveledCompactorOptions{...}\n)\n```\n\n**Compact Method** (lines 1133-1213):\n1. Acquire `cmtx` (compaction mutex)\n2. Compact head blocks in a loop\n3. Truncate WAL\n4. Compact OOO head (if out-of-order data exists)\n5. Compact persisted blocks\n\n**Compaction Loop** (`db.compactBlocks()`, lines 1357-1396):\n```\nwhile true:\n    if head.compactable():\n        break (prioritize head persistence)\n    plan := compactor.Plan(db.dir)\n    if plan is empty:\n        break\n    uid, err := compactor.Compact(db.dir, plan, db.blocks)\n    reload blocks (delete old, load new)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Special Features\n\n### **Out-of-Order (OOO) Compaction**\n- Separate path: `compactOOOHead()` in `db.go:1238-1282`\n- Uses `OOOCompactionHead` to isolate OOO samples\n- Creates blocks marked with `CompactionHintFromOutOfOrder`\n- Separate cleanup via `truncateOOO()`\n\n### **Overlapping Block Handling**\n- Vertical compaction merges overlapping time ranges\n- Requires `EnableOverlappingCompaction = true` (always in Prometheus)\n- Uses custom `VerticalChunkSeriesMergeFunc` (default: `NewCompactingChunkSeriesMerger`)\n\n### **Tombstone Cleanup**\n- Via `CleanTombstones()` in `db.go:2105-2157`\n- Recompacts blocks to physically remove deleted data\n- Runs iteratively until no tombstones remain\n\n---\n\n## 8. {\n   154\u2192\t// PE specifies the postings encoder. It is called when compactor is writing out the postings for a label name/value pair during compaction.\n   155\u2192\t// If it is nil then the default encoder is used. At the moment that is the \"raw\" encoder. See index.EncodePostingsRaw for more.\n   156\u2192\tPE index.PostingsEncoder\n   157\u2192\t// MaxBlockChunkSegmentSize is the max block chunk segment size. NewLeveledCompactorWithOptions(ctx context.Context, r prometheus.Registerer, l log.Logger, ranges []int64, pool chunkenc.Pool, opts LeveledCompactorOptions) (*LeveledCompactor, error) {\n 218\u2192\tmeta *BlockMeta\n   219\u2192}\n   220\u2192\n   221\u2192// Plan returns a list of compactable blocks in the provided directory.\n   222\u2192func (c *LeveledCompactor) Plan(dir string) ([]string, error) {\n   223\u2192\tdirs, err := blockDirs(dir)\n   224\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   225\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   226\u2192\t}\n   227\u2192\tif len(dirs) < 1 {\n   228\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil\n   229\u2192\t}\n   230\u2192\n   231\u2192\tvar dms []dirMeta\n   232\u2192\tfor _, dir := range dirs {\n   233\u2192\t\tmeta, _, err := readMetaFile(dir)\n   234\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   235\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   236\u2192\t\t}\n   237\u2192\t\tdms = append(dms, dirMeta{dir, meta})\n   238\u2192\t}\n   239\u2192\treturn c.plan(dms)\n   240\u2192}\n   241\u2192\n   242\u2192func (c *LeveledCompactor) plan(dms []dirMeta) ([]string, error) {\n   243\u2192\tslices.SortFunc(dms, func(a, b dirMeta) int {\n   244\u2192\t\tswitch {\n   245\u2192\t\tcase a.meta.MinTime < b.meta.MinTime:\n   246\u2192\t\t\treturn -1\n   247\u2192\t\tcase a.meta.MinTime > b.meta.MinTime:\n   248\u2192\t\t\treturn 1\n   249\u2192\t\tdefault:\n   250\u2192\t\t\treturn 0\n   251\u2192\t\t}\n   252\u2192\t})\n   253\u2192\n   254\u2192\tres := c.selectOverlappingDirs(dms)\n   255\u2192\tif len(res) > 0 {\n   256\u2192\t\treturn res, nil\n   257\u2192\t}\n   258\u2192\t// No overlapping blocks, do compaction the usual way.\n   259\u2192\t// We do not include a recently created block with max(minTime), so the block which was just created from WAL.\n   260\u2192\t// This gives users a window of a full block size to piece-wise backup new data without having to care about data overlap.\n   261\u2192\tdms = dms[:len(dms)-1]\n   262\u2192\n   263\u2192\tfor _, dm := range c.selectDirs(dms) {\n   264\u2192\t\tres = append(res, dm.dir)\n   265\u2192\t}\n   266\u2192\tif len(res) > 0 {\n   267\u2192\t\treturn res, nil\n   268\u2192\t}\n   269\u2192\n   270\u2192\t// Compact any blocks with big enough time range that have >5% tombstones.\n   271\u2192\tfor i := len(dms) - 1; i >= 0; i-- {\n   272\u2192\t\tmeta := dms[i].meta\n   273\u2192\t\tif meta.MaxTime-meta.MinTime < c.ranges[len(c.ranges)/2] {\n   274\u2192\t\t\t// If the block is entirely deleted, then we don't care about the block being big enough.\n   275\u2192\t\t\t// TODO: This is assuming single tombstone is for distinct series, which might be no true.\n   276\u2192\t\t\tif meta.Stats.NumTombstones > 0 && meta.Stats.NumTombstones >= meta.Stats.NumSeries {\n   277\u2192\t\t\t\treturn []string{dms[i].dir}, nil\n   278\u2192\t\t\t}\n   279\u2192\t\t\tbreak\n   280\u2192\t\t}\n   281\u2192\t\tif float64(meta.Stats.NumTombstones)/float64(meta.Stats.NumSeries+1) > 0.05 {\n   282\u2192\t\t\treturn []string{dms[i].dir}, nil\n   283\u2192\t\t}\n   284\u2192\t}\n   285\u2192\n   286\u2192\treturn nil, nil\n   287\u2192}\n   288\u2192\n   289\u2192// selectDirs returns the dir metas that should be compacted into a single new block.\n   290\u2192// If only a single block range is configured, the result is always nil.\n   291\u2192func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectDirs(ds []dirMeta) []dirMeta {\n   292\u2192\tif len(c.ranges) < 2 || len(ds) < 1 {\n   293\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   294\u2192\t}\n   295\u2192\n   296\u2192\thighTime := ds[len(ds)-1].meta.MinTime\n   297\u2192\n   298\u2192\tfor _, iv := range c.ranges[1:] {\n   299\u2192\t\tparts := splitByRange(ds, iv)\n   300\u2192\t\tif len(parts) == 0 {\n   301\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   302\u2192\t\t}\n   303\u2192\n   304\u2192\tOuter:\n   305\u2192\t\tfor _, p := range parts {\n   306\u2192\t\t\t// Do not select the range if it has a block whose compaction failed.\n   307\u2192\t\t\tfor _, dm := range p {\n   308\u2192\t\t\t\tif dm.meta.Compaction.Failed {\n   309\u2192\t\t\t\t\tcontinue Outer\n   310\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   311\u2192\t\t\t}\n   312\u2192\n   313\u2192\t\t\tmint := p[0].meta.MinTime\n   314\u2192\t\t\tmaxt := p[len(p)-1].meta.MaxTime\n   315\u2192\t\t\t// Pick the range of blocks if it spans the full range (potentially with gaps)\n   316\u2192\t\t\t// or is before the most recent block.\n   317\u2192\t\t\t// This ensures we don't compact blocks prematurely when another one of the same\n   318\u2192\t\t\t// size still fits in the range.\n   319\u2192\t\t\tif (maxt-mint == iv || maxt <= highTime) && len(p) > 1 {\n   320\u2192\t\t\t\treturn p\n   321\u2192\t\t\t}\n   322\u2192\t\t}\n   323\u2192\t}\n   324\u2192\n   325\u2192\treturn nil\n   326\u2192}\n   327\u2192\n   328\u2192// selectOverlappingDirs returns all dirs with overlapping time ranges.\n   329\u2192// It expects sorted input by mint and returns the overlapping dirs in the same order as received.\n   330\u2192func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectOverlappingDirs(ds []dirMeta) []string {\n   331\u2192\tif !c.enableOverlappingCompaction {\n   332\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   333\u2192\t}\n   334\u2192\tif len(ds) < 2 {\n   335\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   336\u2192\t}\n   337\u2192\tvar overlappingDirs []string\n   338\u2192\tglobalMaxt := ds[0].meta.MaxTime\n   339\u2192\tfor i, d := range ds[1:] {\n   340\u2192\t\tif d.meta.MinTime < globalMaxt {\n   341\u2192\t\t\tif len(overlappingDirs) == 0 { // When it is the first overlap, need to add the last one as well.\n   342\u2192\t\t\t\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, ds[i].dir)\n   343\u2192\t\t\t}\n   344\u2192\t\t\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, d.dir)\n   345\u2192\t\t} else if len(overlappingDirs) > 0 {\n   346\u2192\t\t\tbreak\n   347\u2192\t\t}\n   348\u2192\t\tif d.meta.MaxTime > globalMaxt {\n   349\u2192\t\t\tglobalMaxt = d.meta.MaxTime\n   350\u2192\t\t}\n   351\u2192\t}\n   352\u2192\treturn overlappingDirs\n   353\u2192}\n   354\u2192\n   355\u2192// splitByRange splits the directories by the time range. The range sequence starts at 0.\n   356\u2192//\n   357\u2192// For example, if we have blocks [0-10, 10-20, 50-60, 90-100] and the split range tr is 30\n   358\u2192// it returns [0-10, 10-20], [50-60], [90-100].\n   359\u2192func splitByRange(ds []dirMeta, tr int64) [][]dirMeta {\n   360\u2192\tvar splitDirs [][]dirMeta\n   361\u2192\n   362\u2192\tfor i := 0; i < len(ds); {\n   363\u2192\t\tvar (\n   364\u2192\t\t\tgroup []dirMeta\n   365\u2192\t\t\tt0    int64\n   366\u2192\t\t\tm     = ds[i].meta\n   367\u2192\t\t)\n   368\u2192\t\t// Compute start of aligned time range of size tr closest to the current block's start.\n   369\u2192\t\tif m.MinTime >= 0 {\n   370\u2192\t\t\tt0 = tr * (m.MinTime / tr)\n   371\u2192\t\t} else {\n   372\u2192\t\t\tt0 = tr * ((m.MinTime - tr + 1) / tr)\n   373\u2192\t\t}\n   374\u2192\t\t// Skip blocks that don't fall into the range. This can happen via mis-alignment or\n   375\u2192\t\t// by being the multiple of the intended range.\n   376\u2192\t\tif m.MaxTime > t0+tr {\n   377\u2192\t\t\ti++\n   378\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   379\u2192\t\t}\n   380\u2192\n   381\u2192\t\t// Add all dirs to the current group that are within [t0, t0+tr].\n   382\u2192\t\tfor ; i < len(ds); i++ {\n   383\u2192\t\t\t// Either the block falls into the next range or doesn't fit at all (checked above).\n   384\u2192\t\t\tif ds[i].meta.MaxTime > t0+tr {\n   385\u2192\t\t\t\tbreak\n   386\u2192\t\t\t}\n   387\u2192\t\t\tgroup = append(group, ds[i])\n   388\u2192\t\t}\n   389\u2192\n   390\u2192\t\tif len(group) > 0 {\n   391\u2192\t\t\tsplitDirs = append(splitDirs, group)\n   392\u2192\t\t}\n   393\u2192\t}\n   394\u2192\n   395\u2192\treturn splitDirs\n   396\u2192}\n   397\u2192\n   398\u2192// CompactBlockMetas merges many block metas into one, combining it's source blocks together\n   399\u2192// and adjusting compaction level. Min/Max time of result block meta covers all input blocks.\n   400\u2192func CompactBlockMetas(uid ulid.ULID, blocks ...*BlockMeta) *BlockMeta {\n   401\u2192\tres := &BlockMeta{\n   402\u2192\t\tULID: uid,\n   403\u2192\t}\n   404\u2192\n   405\u2192\tsources := map[ulid.ULID]struct{}{}\n   406\u2192\tmint := blocks[0].MinTime\n   407\u2192\tmaxt := blocks[0].MaxTime\n   408\u2192\n   409\u2192\tfor _, b := range blocks {\n   410\u2192\t\tif b.MinTime < mint {\n   411\u2192\t\t\tmint = b.MinTime\n   412\u2192\t\t}\n   413\u2192\t\tif b.MaxTime > maxt {\n   414\u2192\t\t\tmaxt = b.MaxTime\n   415\u2192\t\t}\n   416\u2192\t\tif b.Compaction.Level > res.Compaction.Level {\n   417\u2192\t\t\tres.Compaction.Level = b.Compaction.Level\n   418\u2192\t\t}\n   419\u2192\t\tfor _, s := range b.Compaction.Sources {\n   420\u2192\t\t\tsources[s] = struct{}{}\n   421\u2192\t\t}\n   422\u2192\t\tres.Compaction.Parents = append(res.Compaction.Parents, BlockDesc{\n   423\u2192\t\t\tULID:    b.ULID,\n   424\u2192\t\t\tMinTime: b.MinTime,\n   425\u2192\t\t\tMaxTime: b.MaxTime,\n   426\u2192\t\t})\n   427\u2192\t}\n   428\u2192\tres.Compaction.Level++\n   429\u2192\n   430\u2192\tfor s := range sources {\n   431\u2192\t\tres.Compaction.Sources = append(res.Compaction.Sources, s)\n   432\u2192\t}\n   433\u2192\tslices.SortFunc(res.Compaction.Sources, func(a, b ulid.ULID) int {\n   434\u2192\t\treturn a.Compare(b)\n   435\u2192\t})\n   436\u2192\n   437\u2192\tres.MinTime = mint\n   438\u2192\tres.MaxTime = maxt\n   439\u2192\treturn res\n   440\u2192}\n   441\u2192\n   442\u2192// Compact creates a new block in the compactor's directory from the blocks in the\n   443\u2192// provided directories.\n   444\u2192func (c *LeveledCompactor) Compact(dest string, dirs []string, open []*Block) (uid ulid.ULID, err error) {\n   445\u2192\treturn c.CompactWithBlockPopulator(dest, BlockPopulator) (uid ulid.ULID, err error) {\n   449\u2192\tvar (\n   450\u2192\t\tblocks []BlockReader\n   451\u2192\t\tbs     []*Block\n   452\u2192\t\tmetas  []*BlockMeta\n   453\u2192\t\tuids *LeveledCompactor) Write(dest string, b BlockReader, mint, maxt int64, base *BlockMeta) (ulid.ULID, error) {\n   540\u2192\tstart := time.Now()\n   541\u2192\n   542\u2192\tuid := (wal files) max size.\n    93\u2192\t// WALSegmentSize = 0, segment size is default size.\n    94\u2192\t// WALSegmentSize > 0, segment size is WALSegmentSize.\n    95\u2192\t// WALSegmentSize < 0, 0, chunk segment size is default size.\n   100\u2192\t// MaxBlockChunkSegmentSize > 0, chunk segment size is MaxBlockChunkSegmentSize.\n   101\u2192\tMaxBlockChunkSegmentSize int64\n   102\u2192\n   103\u2192\t// Duration of persisted data to keep.\n   104\u2192\t// Unit agnostic as long as unit is consistent with MinBlockDuration and MaxBlockDuration.\n   105\u2192\t// Typically it is in milliseconds.\n   106\u2192\tRetentionDuration int64\n   107\u2192\n   108\u2192\t// Maximum number of bytes in blocks to be retained.\n   109\u2192\t// 0 or less means disabled.\n   110\u2192\t// NOTE: For proper storage calculations need to consider\n   111\u2192\t// the size of the WAL folder which is not added when calculating\n   112\u2192\t// the current size of the database.\n processes WAL replay.\n   122\u2192\t// If it is <=0, then GOMAXPROCS is used.\n   123\u2192\tWALReplayConcurrency int\n   124\u2192\n   125\u2192\t// StripeSize is the size in entries of the series hash map. Reducing the size will save memory but impact performance.\n   126\u2192\tStripeSize int\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192\t// The timestamp range of head blocks after which they get persisted.\n   129\u2192\t// It's the minimum duration of any persisted block.\n   130\u2192\t// Unit agnostic as long as unit is consistent with RetentionDuration and MaxBlockDuration.\n   131\u2192\t// Typically consistent with MinBlockDuration and RetentionDuration.\n   136\u2192\t// Typically it is in milliseconds.\n   137\u2192\tMaxBlockDuration int64\n   138\u2192\n   139\u2192\t// samples per chunk.\n   146\u2192\tSamplesPerChunk int\n   147\u2192\n   148\u2192\t// SeriesLifecycleCallback specifies a list of callbacks that will be called during a lifecycle of a series.\n   149\u2192\t// It is always a no-op in Prometheus and mainly meant for external users who import TSDB.\n   150\u2192\tSeriesLifecycleCallback SeriesLifecycleCallback\n   151\u2192\n   152\u2192\t// for external users who import TSDB.\n   155\u2192\tBlocksToDelete BlocksToDeleteFunc\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192\t// Enables the in memory exemplar storage.\n   158\u2192\tEnableExemplarStorage bool\n   159\u2192\n   160\u2192\t// Enables the snapshot of in-memory chunks on shutdown. This makes restarts faster.\n   161\u2192\tEnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown bool\n   162\u2192\n   163\u2192\t// MaxExemplars sets the size, in # of exemplars stored, of the single circular buffer used to store exemplars in memory.\n   164\u2192\t// See tsdb/exemplar.go, specifically the CircularExemplarStorage struct and it's constructor NewCircularExemplarStorage.\n   165\u2192\tMaxExemplars int64\n   166\u2192\n   167\u2192\t// Disables isolation between reads and in-flight appends.\n   168\u2192\tIsolationDisabled bool\n   169\u2192\n   170\u2192\t// EnableNativeHistograms enables the ingestion of native histograms.\n   171\u2192\tEnableNativeHistograms bool\n   172\u2192\n   173\u2192\t// OutOfOrderTimeWindow specifies how much out of order is allowed, if any.\n   174\u2192\t// This can change during run-time, so this value from here should only be used\n   175\u2192\t// while initialising.\n   176\u2192\tOutOfOrderTimeWindow int64\n   177\u2192\n   178\u2192\t// OutOfOrderCapMax is maximum capacity for OOO chunks (in samples).\n   179\u2192\t// If it is <=0, the default value is assumed.\n   180\u2192\tOutOfOrderCapMax int64\n   181\u2192\n   182\u2192\t// Compaction of overlapping blocks are allowed if EnableOverlappingCompaction is true.\n   183\u2192\t// This is an optional flag for overlapping blocks.\n   184\u2192\t// The reason why this flag exists is because there are various users of the TSDB\n   185\u2192\t// that do not want vertical compaction happening on ingest time.  344\u2192\tif r != nil {\n   345\u2192\t\tr.MustRegister(\n   346\u2192\t\t\tm.loadedBlocks,\n   347\u2192\t\t\tm.symbolTableSize,\n   348\u2192\t\t\tm.reloads,\n   349\u2192\t\t\tm.reloadsFailed,\n   350\u2192\t\t\tm.compactionsFailed,\n   351\u2192\t\t\tm.compactionsTriggered,\n   352\u2192\t\t\tm.compactionsSkipped,\n   353\u2192\t\t\tm.sizeRetentionCount,\n   354\u2192\t\t\tm.timeRetentionCount,\n   355\u2192\t\t\tm.startTime,\n   356\u2192\t\t\tm.tombCleanTimer,\n   357\u2192\t\t\tm.blocksBytes,\n   358\u2192\t\t\tm.maxBytes,\n   359\u2192\t\t\tm.retentionDuration,\n   360\u2192\t\t)\n   361\u2192\t}\n   362\u2192\treturn m\n   363\u2192}\n   364\u2192\n   365\u2192// DBStats contains statistics about the DB separated by component (eg. head).\n   366\u2192// They are available before the DB has finished initializing.\n   367\u2192type DBStats struct {\n   368\u2192\tHead *HeadStats\n   369\u2192}\n   370\u2192\n   371\u2192// NewDBStats returns a new DBStats object initialized using the\n   372\u2192// new function from each component.\n   373\u2192func NewDBStats() *DBStats {\n   374\u2192\treturn &DBStats{\n   375\u2192\t\tHead: NewHeadStats(),\n   376\u2192\t}\n   377\u2192}\n   378\u2192\n   379\u2192// ErrClosed is returned when the db is closed.\n   380\u2192var ErrClosed = errors.New(\"db already closed\")\n   381\u2192\n   382\u2192// DBReadOnly provides APIs for read only operations on a database.\n   383\u2192// Current implementation doesn't support concurrency so\n   384\u2192// all API calls should happen in the same go routine.\n   385\u2192type DBReadOnly struct {\n   386\u2192\tlogger  log.Logger\n   387\u2192\tdir     string\n   388\u2192\tclosers []io.Closer\n   389\u2192\tclosed  chan struct{}\n   390\u2192}\n   391\u2192\n   392\u2192// OpenDBReadOnly opens DB in the given directory for read only operations.\n   393\u2192func OpenDBReadOnly(dir string, l log.Logger) (*DBReadOnly, error) {\n   394\u2192\tif _, err := os.Stat(dir); err != nil {\n   395\u2192\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"opening the db dir: %w\", err)\n   396\u2192\t}\n   397\u2192\n   398\u2192\tif l == nil {\n   399\u2192\t\tl = log.NewNopLogger()\n   400\u2192\t}\n   401\u2192\n   402\u2192\treturn &DBReadOnly{\n   403\u2192\t\tlogger: l,\n   404\u2192\t\tdir:    dir,\n   405\u2192\t\tclosed: make(chan struct{}),\n   406\u2192\t}, nil\n   407\u2192}\n   408\u2192\n   409\u2192// FlushWAL creates a new block containing all data that's currently in the memory buffer/WAL.\n   410\u2192// Samples that are in existing blocks will not be written to the new block.\n   411\u2192// Note that if the read only database is running concurrently with a\n   412\u2192// writable database then writing the WAL to the database directory can race.\n   413\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) FlushWAL(dir string) (returnErr error) {\n   414\u2192\tblockReaders, err := db.Blocks()\n   415\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   416\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"read blocks: %w\", err)\n   417\u2192\t}\n   418\u2192\tmaxBlockTime := int64(math.MinInt64)\n   419\u2192\tif len(blockReaders) > 0 {\n   420\u2192\t\tmaxBlockTime = blockReaders[len(blockReaders)-1].Meta().MaxTime\n   421\u2192\t}\n   422\u2192\tw, err := wlog.Open(db.logger, filepath.Join(db.dir, \"wal\"))\n   423\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   424\u2192\t\treturn err\n   425\u2192\t}\n   426\u2192\tvar wbl *wlog.WL\n   427\u2192\twblDir := filepath.Join(db.dir, wlog.WblDirName)\n   428\u2192\tif _, err := os.Stat(wblDir); !os.IsNotExist(err) {\n   429\u2192\t\twbl, err = wlog.Open(db.logger, wblDir)\n   430\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   431\u2192\t\t\treturn err\n   432\u2192\t\t}\n   433\u2192\t}\n   434\u2192\topts := DefaultHeadOptions()\n   435\u2192\topts.ChunkDirRoot = db.dir\n   436\u2192\thead, err := NewHead(nil, db.logger, w, wbl, opts, NewHeadStats())\n   437\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   438\u2192\t\treturn err\n   439\u2192\t}\n   440\u2192\tdefer func() {\n   441\u2192\t\terrs := tsdb_errors.NewMulti(returnErr)\n   442\u2192\t\tif err := head.Close(); err != nil {\n   443\u2192\t\t\terrs.Add(fmt.Errorf(\"closing Head: %w\", err))\n   444\u2192\t\t}\n   445\u2192\t\treturnErr = errs.Err()\n   446\u2192\t}()\n   447\u2192\t// Set the min valid time for the ingested wal samples\n   448\u2192\t// to be no lower than the maxt of the last block.\n   449\u2192\tif err := head.Init(maxBlockTime); err != nil {\n   450\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"read WAL: %w\", err)\n   451\u2192\t}\n   452\u2192\tmint := head.MinTime()\n   453\u2192\tmaxt := head.MaxTime()\n   454\u2192\trh := NewRangeHead(head, mint, maxt)\n   455\u2192\tcompactor, err := NewLeveledCompactor(\n   456\u2192\t\tcontext.Background(),\n   457\u2192\t\tnil,\n   458\u2192\t\tdb.logger,\n   459\u2192\t\tExponentialBlockRanges(DefaultOptions().MinBlockDuration, 3, 5),\n   460\u2192\t\tchunkenc.NewPool(), nil,\n   461\u2192\t)\n   462\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   463\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"create leveled compactor: %w\", err)\n   464\u2192\t}\n   465\u2192\t// Add +1 millisecond to block maxt because block intervals are half-open: [b.MinTime, b.MaxTime).\n   466\u2192\t// Because of this block intervals are always +1 than the total samples it includes.\n   467\u2192\t_, err = compactor.Write(dir, rh, mint, maxt+1, nil)\n   468\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   469\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"writing WAL: %w\", err)\n   470\u2192\t}\n   471\u2192\treturn nil\n   472\u2192}\n   473\u2192\n   474\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) loadDataAsQueryable(maxt int64) (storage.SampleAndChunkQueryable, error) {\n   475\u2192\tselect {\n   476\u2192\tcase <-db.closed:\n   477\u2192\t\treturn nil, ErrClosed\n   478\u2192\tdefault:\n   479\u2192\t}\n   480\u2192\tblockReaders, err := db.Blocks()\n   481\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   482\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   483\u2192\t}\n   484\u2192\tblocks := make([]*Block, len(blockReaders))\n   485\u2192\tfor i, b := range blockReaders {\n   486\u2192\t\tb, ok := b.(*Block)\n   487\u2192\t\tif !ok {\n   488\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"unable to convert a read only block to a normal block\")\n   489\u2192\t\t}\n   490\u2192\t\tblocks[i] = b\n   491\u2192\t}\n   492\u2192\n   493\u2192\topts := DefaultHeadOptions()\n   494\u2192\topts.ChunkDirRoot = db.dir\n   495\u2192\thead, err := NewHead(nil, db.logger, nil, nil, opts, NewHeadStats())\n   496\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   497\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   498\u2192\t}\n   499\u2192\tmaxBlockTime := int64(math.MinInt64)\n   500\u2192\tif len(blocks) > 0 {\n   501\u2192\t\tmaxBlockTime = blocks[len(blocks)-1].Meta().MaxTime\n   502\u2192\t}\n   503\u2192\n   504\u2192\t// Also add the WAL if the current blocks don't cover the requests time range.\n   505\u2192\tif maxBlockTime <= maxt {\n   506\u2192\t\tif err := head.Close(); err != nil {\n   507\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   508\u2192\t\t}\n   509\u2192\t\tw, err := wlog.Open(db.logger, filepath.Join(db.dir, \"wal\"))\n   510\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   511\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   512\u2192\t\t}\n   513\u2192\t\tvar wbl *wlog.WL\n   514\u2192\t\twblDir := filepath.Join(db.dir, wlog.WblDirName)\n   515\u2192\t\tif _, err := os.Stat(wblDir); !os.IsNotExist(err) {\n   516\u2192\t\t\twbl, err = wlog.Open(db.logger, wblDir)\n   517\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   518\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   519\u2192\t\t\t}\n   520\u2192\t\t}\n   521\u2192\t\topts := DefaultHeadOptions()\n   522\u2192\t\topts.ChunkDirRoot = db.dir\n   523\u2192\t\thead, err = NewHead(nil, db.logger, w, wbl, opts, NewHeadStats())\n   524\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   525\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   526\u2192\t\t}\n   527\u2192\t\t// Set the min valid time for the ingested wal samples\n   528\u2192\t\t// to be no lower than the maxt of the last block.\n   529\u2192\t\tif err := head.Init(maxBlockTime); err != nil {\n   530\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"read WAL: %w\", err)\n   531\u2192\t\t}\n   532\u2192\t\t// Set the wal and the wbl to nil to disable related operations.\n   533\u2192\t\t// This is mainly to avoid blocking when closing the head.\n   534\u2192\t\thead.wal = nil\n   535\u2192\t\thead.wbl = nil\n   536\u2192\t}\n   537\u2192\n   538\u2192\tdb.closers = append(db.closers, head)\n   539\u2192\treturn &DB{\n   540\u2192\t\tdir:    db.dir,\n   541\u2192\t\tlogger: db.logger,\n   542\u2192\t\tblocks: blocks,\n   543\u2192\t\thead:   head,\n   544\u2192\t}, nil\n   545\u2192}\n   546\u2192\n   547\u2192// Querier loads the blocks and wal and returns a new querier over the data partition for the given time range.\n   548\u2192// Current implementation doesn't support multiple Queriers.\n   549\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) Querier(mint, maxt int64) (storage.Querier, error) {\n   550\u2192\tq, err := db.loadDataAsQueryable(maxt)\n   551\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   552\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   553\u2192\t}\n   554\u2192\treturn q.Querier(mint, maxt)\n   555\u2192}\n   556\u2192\n   557\u2192// ChunkQuerier loads blocks and the wal and returns a new chunk querier over the data partition for the given time range.\n   558\u2192// Current implementation doesn't support multiple ChunkQueriers.\n   559\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) ChunkQuerier(mint, maxt int64) (storage.ChunkQuerier, error) {\n   560\u2192\tq, err := db.loadDataAsQueryable(maxt)\n   561\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   562\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   563\u2192\t}\n   564\u2192\treturn q.ChunkQuerier(mint, maxt)\n   565\u2192}\n   566\u2192\n   567\u2192// Blocks returns a slice of block readers for persisted blocks.\n   568\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) Blocks() ([]BlockReader, error) {\n   569\u2192\tselect {\n   570\u2192\tcase <-db.closed:\n   571\u2192\t\treturn nil, ErrClosed\n   572\u2192\tdefault:\n   573\u2192\t}\n   574\u2192\tloadable, corrupted, err := openBlocks(db.logger, db.dir, nil, nil)\n   575\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   576\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   577\u2192\t}\n   578\u2192\n   579\u2192\t// Corrupted blocks that have been superseded by a loadable block can be safely ignored.\n   580\u2192\tfor _, block := range loadable {\n   581\u2192\t\tfor _, b := range block.Meta().Compaction.Parents {\n   582\u2192\t\t\tdelete(corrupted, b.ULID)\n   583\u2192\t\t}\n   584\u2192\t}\n   585\u2192\tif len(corrupted) > 0 {\n   586\u2192\t\tfor _, b := range loadable {\n   587\u2192\t\t\tif err := b.Close(); err != nil {\n   588\u2192\t\t\t\tlevel.Warn(db.logger).Log(\"msg\", \"Closing block failed\", \"err\", err, \"block\", b)\n   589\u2192\t\t\t}\n   590\u2192\t\t}\n   591\u2192\t\terrs := tsdb_errors.NewMulti()\n   592\u2192\t\tfor ulid, err := range corrupted {\n   593\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   594\u2192\t\t\t\terrs.Add(fmt.Errorf(\"corrupted block %s: %w\", ulid.String(), err))\n   595\u2192\t\t\t}\n   596\u2192\t\t}\n   597\u2192\t\treturn nil, errs.Err()\n   598\u2192\t}\n   599\u2192\n   600\u2192\tif len(loadable) == 0 {\n   601\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil\n   602\u2192\t}\n   603\u2192\n   604\u2192\tslices.SortFunc(loadable, func(a, b *Block) int {\n   605\u2192\t\tswitch {\n   606\u2192\t\tcase a.Meta().MinTime < b.Meta().MinTime:\n   607\u2192\t\t\treturn -1\n   608\u2192\t\tcase a.Meta().MinTime > b.Meta().MinTime:\n   609\u2192\t\t\treturn 1\n   610\u2192\t\tdefault:\n   611\u2192\t\t\treturn 0\n   612\u2192\t\t}\n   613\u2192\t})\n   614\u2192\n   615\u2192\tblockMetas := make([]BlockMeta, 0, len(loadable))\n   616\u2192\tfor _, b := range loadable {\n   617\u2192\t\tblockMetas = append(blockMetas, b.Meta())\n   618\u2192\t}\n   619\u2192\tif overlaps := OverlappingBlocks(blockMetas); len(overlaps) > 0 {\n   620\u2192\t\tlevel.Warn(db.logger).Log(\"msg\", \"Overlapping blocks found during opening\", \"detail\", overlaps.String())\n   621\u2192\t}\n   622\u2192\n   623\u2192\t// Close all previously open readers and add the new ones to the cache.\n   624\u2192\tfor _, closer := range db.closers {\n   625\u2192\t\tcloser.Close()\n   626\u2192\t}\n   627\u2192\n   628\u2192\tblockClosers := make([]io.Closer, len(loadable))\n   629\u2192\tblockReaders := make([]BlockReader, len(loadable))\n   630\u2192\tfor i, b := range loadable {\n   631\u2192\t\tblockClosers[i] = b\n   632\u2192\t\tblockReaders[i] = b\n   633\u2192\t}\n   634\u2192\tdb.closers = blockClosers\n   635\u2192\n   636\u2192\treturn blockReaders, nil\n   637\u2192}\n   638\u2192\n   639\u2192// LastBlockID returns the BlockID of latest block.\n   640\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) LastBlockID() (string, error) {\n   641\u2192\tentries, err := os.ReadDir(db.dir)\n   642\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   643\u2192\t\treturn \"\", err\n   644\u2192\t}\n   645\u2192\n   646\u2192\tmax := uint64(0)\n   647\u2192\n   648\u2192\tlastBlockID := \"\"\n   649\u2192\n   650\u2192\tfor _, e := range entries {\n   651\u2192\t\t// Check if dir is a block dir or not.\n   652\u2192\t\tdirName := e.Name()\n   653\u2192\t\tulidObj, err := ulid.ParseStrict(dirName)\n   654\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   655\u2192\t\t\tcontinue // Not a block dir.\n   656\u2192\t\t}\n   657\u2192\t\ttimestamp := ulidObj.Time()\n   658\u2192\t\tif timestamp > max {\n   659\u2192\t\t\tmax = timestamp\n   660\u2192\t\t\tlastBlockID = dirName\n   661\u2192\t\t}\n   662\u2192\t}\n   663\u2192\n   664\u2192\tif lastBlockID == \"\" {\n   665\u2192\t\treturn \"\", errors.New(\"no blocks found\")\n   666\u2192\t}\n   667\u2192\n   668\u2192\treturn lastBlockID, nil\n   669\u2192}\n   670\u2192\n   671\u2192// Block returns a block reader by given block id.\n   672\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) Block(blockID string) (BlockReader, error) {\n   673\u2192\tselect {\n   674\u2192\tcase <-db.closed:\n   675\u2192\t\treturn nil, ErrClosed\n   676\u2192\tdefault:\n   677\u2192\t}\n   678\u2192\n   679\u2192\t_, err := os.Stat(filepath.Join(db.dir, blockID))\n   680\u2192\tif os.IsNotExist(err) {\n   681\u2192\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid block ID %s\", blockID)\n   682\u2192\t}\n   683\u2192\n   684\u2192\tblock, err := OpenBlock(db.logger, filepath.Join(db.dir, blockID), nil)\n   685\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   686\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   687\u2192\t}\n   688\u2192\tdb.closers = append(db.closers, block)\n   689\u2192\n   690\u2192\treturn block, nil\n   691\u2192}\n   692\u2192\n   693\u2192// Close all block readers.\n   694\u2192func (db *DBReadOnly) Close() error {\n   695\u2192\tselect {\n   696\u2192\tcase <-db.closed:\n   697\u2192\t\treturn ErrClosed\n   698\u2192\tdefault:\n   699\u2192\t}\n   700\u2192\tclose(db.closed)\n   701\u2192\n   702\u2192\treturn tsdb_errors.CloseAll(db.closers)\n   703\u2192}\n   704\u2192\n   705\u2192// Open returns a new DB in the given directory. If options are empty, DefaultOptions will be used.\n   706\u2192func Open(dir string, l log.Logger, r prometheus.Registerer, opts *Options, stats *DBStats) (db *DB, err error) {\n   707\u2192\tvar rngs []int64\n   708\u2192\topts, rngs = validateOpts(opts, nil)\n   709\u2192\n   710\u2192\treturn open(dir, l, r, opts, rngs, stats)\n   711\u2192}\n   712\u2192\n   713\u2192func validateOpts(opts *Options, rngs []int64) (*Options, []int64) {\n   714\u2192\tif opts == nil {\n   715\u2192\t\topts = DefaultOptions()\n   716\u2192\t}\n   717\u2192\tif opts.StripeSize <= 0 {\n   718\u2192\t\topts.StripeSize = DefaultStripeSize\n   719\u2192\t}\n   720\u2192\tif opts.HeadChunksWriteBufferSize <= 0 {\n   721\u2192\t\topts.HeadChunksWriteBufferSize = chunks.DefaultWriteBufferSize\n   722\u2192\t}\n   723\u2192\tif opts.HeadChunksWriteQueueSize < 0 {\n   724\u2192\t\topts.HeadChunksWriteQueueSize = chunks.DefaultWriteQueueSize\n   725\u2192\t}\n   726\u2192\tif opts.SamplesPerChunk <= 0 {\n   727\u2192\t\topts.SamplesPerChunk = DefaultSamplesPerChunk\n   728\u2192\t}\n   729\u2192\tif opts.MaxBlockChunkSegmentSize <= 0 {\n   730\u2192\t\topts.MaxBlockChunkSegmentSize = chunks.DefaultChunkSegmentSize\n   731\u2192\t}\n   732\u2192\tif opts.MinBlockDuration <= 0 {\n   733\u2192\t\topts.MinBlockDuration = DefaultBlockDuration\n   734\u2192\t}\n   735\u2192\tif opts.MinBlockDuration > opts.MaxBlockDuration {\n   736\u2192\t\topts.MaxBlockDuration = opts.MinBlockDuration\n   737\u2192\t}\n   738\u2192\tif opts.OutOfOrderCapMax <= 0 {\n   739\u2192\t\topts.OutOfOrderCapMax = DefaultOutOfOrderCapMax\n   740\u2192\t}\n   741\u2192\tif opts.OutOfOrderTimeWindow < 0 {\n   742\u2192\t\topts.OutOfOrderTimeWindow = 0\n   743\u2192\t}\n   744\u2192\n   745\u2192\tif len(rngs) == 0 {\n   746\u2192\t\t// Start with smallest block duration and create exponential buckets until the exceed the\n   747\u2192\t\t// configured maximum block duration.\n   748\u2192\t\trngs = ExponentialBlockRanges(opts.MinBlockDuration, 10, 3)\n   749\u2192\t}\n   750\u2192\treturn opts, rngs\n   751\u2192}\n   752\u2192\n   753\u2192// open returns a new DB in the given directory.\n   754\u2192// It initializes the lockfile, WAL, compactor, and Head (by replaying the WAL), and runs the database.\n   755\u2192// It is not safe to open more than one DB in the same directory.\n   756\u2192func open(dir string, l log.Logger, r prometheus.Registerer, opts *Options, rngs []int64, stats *DBStats) (_ *DB, returnedErr error) {\n   757\u2192\tif err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o777); err != nil {\n   758\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   759\u2192\t}\n   760\u2192\tif l == nil {\n   761\u2192\t\tl = log.NewNopLogger()\n   762\u2192\t}\n   763\u2192\tif stats == nil {\n   764\u2192\t\tstats = NewDBStats()\n   765\u2192\t}\n   766\u2192\n   767\u2192\tfor i, v := range rngs {\n   768\u2192\t\tif v > opts.MaxBlockDuration {\n   769\u2192\t\t\trngs = rngs[:i]\n   770\u2192\t\t\tbreak\n   771\u2192\t\t}\n   772\u2192\t}\n   773\u2192\n   774\u2192\t// Fixup bad format written by Prometheus 2.1.\n   775\u2192\tif err := repairBadIndexVersion(l, dir); err != nil {\n   776\u2192\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"repair bad index version: %w\", err)\n   777\u2192\t}\n   778\u2192\n   779\u2192\twalDir := filepath.Join(dir, \"wal\")\n   780\u2192\twblDir := filepath.Join(dir, wlog.WblDirName)\n   781\u2192\n   782\u2192\tfor _, tmpDir := range []string{walDir, dir} {\n   783\u2192\t\t// Remove tmp dirs.\n   784\u2192\t\tif err := removeBestEffortTmpDirs(l, tmpDir); err != nil {\n   785\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"remove tmp dirs: %w\", err)\n   786\u2192\t\t}\n   787\u2192\t}\n   788\u2192\n   789\u2192\tdb := &DB{\n   790\u2192\t\tdir:            dir,\n   791\u2192\t\tlogger:         l,\n   792\u2192\t\topts:           opts,\n   793\u2192\t\tcompactc:       make(chan struct{}, 1),\n   794\u2192\t\tdonec:          make(chan struct{}),\n   795\u2192\t\tstopc:          make(chan struct{}),\n   796\u2192\t\tautoCompact:    true,\n   797\u2192\t\tchunkPool:      chunkenc.NewPool(),\n   798\u2192\t\tblocksToDelete: opts.BlocksToDelete,\n   799\u2192\t\tregisterer:     r,\n   800\u2192\t}\n   801\u2192\tdefer func() {\n   802\u2192\t\t// Close files if startup fails somewhere.\n   803\u2192\t\tif returnedErr == nil {\n   804\u2192\t\t\treturn\n   805\u2192\t\t}\n   806\u2192\n   807\u2192\t\tclose(db.donec) // DB is never run if it was an error, so close this channel here.\n   808\u2192\t\terrs := tsdb_errors.NewMulti(returnedErr)\n   809\u2192\t\tif err := db.Close(); err != nil {\n   810\u2192\t\t\terrs.Add(fmt.Errorf(\"close DB after failed startup: %w\", err))\n   811\u2192\t\t}\n   812\u2192\t\treturnedErr = errs.Err()\n   813\u2192\t}()\n   814\u2192\n   815\u2192\tif db.blocksToDelete == nil {\n   816\u2192\t\tdb.blocksToDelete = DefaultBlocksToDelete(db)\n   817\u2192\t}\n   818\u2192\n   819\u2192\tvar err error\n   820\u2192\tdb.locker, err = tsdbutil.NewDirLocker(dir, \"tsdb\", db.logger, r)\n   821\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   822\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   823\u2192\t}\n   824\u2192\tif !opts.NoLockfile {\n   825\u2192\t\tif err := db.locker.Lock(); err != nil {\n   826\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   827\u2192\t\t}\n   828\u2192\t}\n   829\u2192\n   830\u2192\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n   831\u2192\tdb.compactor, err = NewLeveledCompactorWithOptions(ctx, r, l, rngs, db.chunkPool, LeveledCompactorOptions{\n   832\u2192\t\tMaxBlockChunkSegmentSize:    opts.MaxBlockChunkSegmentSize,\n   833\u2192\t\tEnableOverlappingCompaction: opts.EnableOverlappingCompaction,\n   834\u2192\t})\n   835\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   836\u2192\t\tcancel()\n   837\u2192\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"create leveled compactor: %w\", err)\n   838\u2192\t}\n   839\u2192\tdb.compactCancel = cancel\n   840\u2192\n   841\u2192\tvar wal, wbl *wlog.WL\n   842\u2192\tsegmentSize := wlog.DefaultSegmentSize\n   843\u2192\t// Wal is enabled.\n   844\u2192\tif opts.WALSegmentSize >= 0 {\n   845\u2192\t\t// Wal is set to a custom size.\n   846\u2192\t\tif opts.WALSegmentSize > 0 {\n   847\u2192\t\t\tsegmentSize = opts.WALSegmentSize\n   848\u2192\t\t}\n   849\u2192\t\twal, err = wlog.NewSize(l, r, walDir, segmentSize, opts.WALCompression)\n   850\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   851\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   852\u2192\t\t}\n   853\u2192\t\t// Check if there is a WBL on disk, in which case we should replay that data.\n   854\u2192\t\twblSize, err := fileutil.DirSize(wblDir)\n   855\u2192\t\tif err != nil && !os.IsNotExist(err) {\n   856\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   857\u2192\t\t}\n   858\u2192\t\tif opts.OutOfOrderTimeWindow > 0 || wblSize > 0 {\n   859\u2192\t\t\twbl, err = wlog.NewSize(l, r, wblDir, segmentSize, opts.WALCompression)\n   860\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   861\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   862\u2192\t\t\t}\n   863\u2192\t\t}\n   864\u2192\t}\n   865\u2192\tdb.oooWasEnabled.Store(opts.OutOfOrderTimeWindow > 0)\n   866\u2192\theadOpts := DefaultHeadOptions()\n   867\u2192\theadOpts.ChunkRange = rngs[0]\n   868\u2192\theadOpts.ChunkDirRoot = dir\n   869\u2192\theadOpts.ChunkPool = db.chunkPool\n   870\u2192\theadOpts.ChunkWriteBufferSize = opts.HeadChunksWriteBufferSize\n   871\u2192\theadOpts.ChunkWriteQueueSize = opts.HeadChunksWriteQueueSize\n   872\u2192\theadOpts.SamplesPerChunk = opts.SamplesPerChunk\n   873\u2192\theadOpts.StripeSize = opts.StripeSize\n   874\u2192\theadOpts.SeriesCallback = opts.SeriesLifecycleCallback\n   875\u2192\theadOpts.EnableExemplarStorage = opts.EnableExemplarStorage\n   876\u2192\theadOpts.MaxExemplars.Store(opts.MaxExemplars)\n   877\u2192\theadOpts.EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown = opts.EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown\n   878\u2192\theadOpts.EnableNativeHistograms.Store(opts.EnableNativeHistograms)\n   879\u2192\theadOpts.OutOfOrderTimeWindow.Store(opts.OutOfOrderTimeWindow)\n   880\u2192\theadOpts.OutOfOrderCapMax.Store(opts.OutOfOrderCapMax)\n   881\u2192\theadOpts.EnableSharding = opts.EnableSharding\n   882\u2192\tif opts.WALReplayConcurrency > 0 {\n   883\u2192\t\theadOpts.WALReplayConcurrency = opts.WALReplayConcurrency\n   884\u2192\t}\n   885\u2192\tif opts.IsolationDisabled {\n   886\u2192\t\t// We only override this flag if isolation is disabled at DB level. We use the default otherwise.\n   887\u2192\t\theadOpts.IsolationDisabled = opts.IsolationDisabled\n   888\u2192\t}\n   889\u2192\tdb.head, err = NewHead(r, l, wal, wbl, headOpts, stats.Head)\n   890\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   891\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   892\u2192\t}\n   893\u2192\tdb.head.writeNotified = db.writeNotified\n   894\u2192\n   895\u2192\t// Register metrics after assigning the head block.\n   896\u2192\tdb.metrics = newDBMetrics(db, r)\n   897\u2192\tmaxBytes := opts.MaxBytes\n   898\u2192\tif maxBytes < 0 {\n   899\u2192\t\tmaxBytes = 0\n   900\u2192\t}\n   901\u2192\tdb.metrics.maxBytes.Set(float64(maxBytes))\n   902\u2192\tdb.metrics.retentionDuration.Set((time.Duration(opts.RetentionDuration) * time.Millisecond).Seconds())\n   903\u2192\n   904\u2192\tif err := db.reload(); err != nil {\n   905\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   906\u2192\t}\n   907\u2192\t// Set the min valid time for the ingested samples\n   908\u2192\t// to be no lower than the maxt of the last block.\n   909\u2192\tminValidTime := int64(math.MinInt64)\n   910\u2192\t// We do not consider blocks created from out-of-order samples for Head's minValidTime\n   911\u2192\t// since minValidTime is only for the in-order data and we do not want to discard unnecessary\n   912\u2192\t// samples from the Head.\n   913\u2192\tinOrderMaxTime, ok := db.inOrderBlocksMaxTime()\n   914\u2192\tif ok {\n   915\u2192\t\tminValidTime = inOrderMaxTime\n   916\u2192\t}\n   917\u2192\n   918\u2192\tif initErr := db.head.Init(minValidTime); initErr != nil {\n   919\u2192\t\tdb.head.metrics.walCorruptionsTotal.Inc()\n   920\u2192\t\tvar e *errLoadWbl\n   921\u2192\t\tif errors.As(initErr, &e) {\n   922\u2192\t\t\tlevel.Warn(db.logger).Log(\"msg\", \"Encountered WBL read error, attempting repair\", \"err\", initErr)\n   923\u2192\t\t\tif err := wbl.Repair(e.err);
