{
  "content": "# Prometheus TSDB Compaction Operational Runbook\n\n## 1. Overview\n\n### Purpose of Compaction\n\nTSDB (Time Series Database) compaction in Prometheus serves three critical functions:\n\n1. **Block Consolidation**: Merges overlapping time blocks to reduce the number of files that need to be queried\n2. **Tombstone Cleanup**: Physically removes series marked for deletion by applying tombstone metadata, reducing disk footprint\n3. **Query Performance**: Maintains optimal query performance by keeping block sizes and levels balanced according to exponential growth\n\nWithout compaction, Prometheus would accumulate small blocks indefinitely, degrading query performance and consuming excessive disk space. Compaction is triggered automatically by Prometheus and typically requires no manual intervention.\n\n### Block Structure and Compaction Levels\n\n**Block Basics**:\n- Each block represents a time-ordered chunk of time series data\n- Blocks have half-open time intervals: `[MinTime, MaxTime)` where MaxTime is exclusive\n- Block structure includes: chunks (samples), index (series metadata), tombstones (deletion markers), meta.json (metadata)\n- Block identifiers are ULIDs (Universally Unique Lexicographically Sortable Identifiers)\n\n**Compaction Levels**:\nPrometheus uses exponential block ranges to organize blocks hierarchically. Given default configuration:\n- **Level 0** (Head blocks): ~2 hours of data from active writes\n- **Level 1**: Result of compacting Level 0 blocks (~6 hours = 3 \u00d7 2h)\n- **Level 2**: Result of compacting Level 1 blocks (~18 hours = 3 \u00d7 6h)\n- **Level 3+**: Continue exponential growth with factor of 3\n\nThis is configured via `DefaultBlockDuration` (2 hours) and exponential step factor (3) in `tsdb/db.go:745-749`.\n\n**Block Metadata Tracking**:\nEach compacted block includes:\n- `Compaction.Level`: How many times this block has been compacted (0=fresh head, 1+=compacted blocks)\n- `Compaction.Sources`: All original head block ULIDs merged into this block\n- `Compaction.Parents`: Direct parent blocks (for tracking lineage during compaction failures)\n- `Compaction.Failed`: Flag indicating if compaction failed (prevents future selection)\n\n### When Compaction is Triggered\n\nCompaction occurs through three independent mechanisms:\n\n#### 1. Head Block Compaction (Time-Based)\n**Condition**: When `(MaxTime - MinTime) > (ChunkRange / 2) * 3` (approximately 3 hours with default 2h chunk range)\n\n**Code Location**: `tsdb/head.go:1630-1639` (`Head.compactable()` method)\n\n**Trigger Pathway**:\n- Periodic check every ~1 minute (DB reload loop in `tsdb/db.go:982-1027`)\n- On-commit signal when samples are appended (`tsdb/db.go:1115-1127`)\n\nWhen the head block meets this threshold, it becomes compactable and will be persisted to disk during the next `DB.Compact()` call.\n\n#### 2. Block-to-Block Compaction (Leveled)\n**Condition**: Multiple blocks at the same compaction level that fit exponential bucket requirements\n\n**Code Location**: `tsdb/compact.go:242-338` (`LeveledCompactor.plan()` method)\n\n**Selection Logic**:\n- Identifies overlapping blocks first (vertical compaction)\n- For non-overlapping blocks: groups by time range and compacts full exponential levels\n- Skips blocks with previous compaction failures (marked `Compaction.Failed = true`)\n- Always excludes the most recent block (preserves write window)\n\n#### 3. Tombstone Cleanup Compaction\n**Condition**: Blocks with >5% of samples deleted via tombstones\n\n**Code Location**: `tsdb/compact.go:302-315` (tombstone selection logic)\n\nPeriodically triggered via `DB.CleanTombstones()` to reclaim disk space from deleted series.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Monitoring Indicators\n\n### Key Prometheus Metrics\n\nThe following metrics are emitted by the LeveledCompactor and should be monitored continuously. All metrics are registered in `tsdb/compact.go:99-151` (`NewCompactorMetrics()` function).\n\n#### Counter Metrics\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total`**\n- Type: Counter\n- Meaning: Total number of compactions executed (both successful and failed ones that were marked)\n- Alert if: Stopped incrementing for >5 minutes despite active time series writes\n- Indicates: Head blocks are not becoming compactable; potential data accumulation\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_vertical_compactions_total`**\n- Type: Counter\n- Meaning: Number of compactions where overlapping blocks were detected and merged\n- Alert if: Continuously increasing rapidly (>10/minute) indicating chronic overlap\n- Indicates: Block generation may be overlapping more than expected (potential for stuck compaction)\n\n#### Gauge Metrics\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block`**\n- Type: Gauge (0 or 1)\n- Meaning: Set to 1 when actively writing compacted data to disk, 0 otherwise\n- Alert if: Remains 1 for >10 minutes (indicates stuck compaction)\n- Indicates: Compaction write operation is hanging, likely I/O or memory issue\n\n#### Histogram Metrics\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds`**\n- Type: Histogram with exponential buckets (1s to 16384s)\n- Meaning: Wall-clock time to complete a compaction operation\n- Alert if: P99 percentile >5 minutes OR regularly hitting the largest bucket\n- Indicates: System is I/O bound or under memory pressure during compaction\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_size_bytes`**\n- Type: Histogram\n- Meaning: Final byte size of chunks after first-level compaction\n- Alert if: P95 percentile >1MB (indicates potential compression issues)\n- Indicates: Chunks are larger than expected; may affect memory usage\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_samples`**\n- Type: Histogram\n- Meaning: Number of samples per chunk after first-level compaction\n- Alert if: P95 percentile >5000 (typical is 500-2000)\n- Indicates: High-cardinality or high-resolution data; normal for certain workloads\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_range_seconds`**\n- Type: Histogram\n- Meaning: Time range covered per chunk after compaction\n- Alert if: P95 percentile significantly <7200s (2 hours), indicating early chunk boundary crossing\n- Indicates: Chunks may be too granular; query performance could be affected\n\n### Related Database Metrics\n\nMonitor alongside compaction metrics:\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded`**\n- Number of currently loaded blocks; should be relatively stable\n- Increase during compaction (new blocks loaded), then decrease (old blocks deleted)\n- Alert if: Remains elevated after compaction completes (failed cleanup)\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_block_truncations_total`**\n- Blocks deleted due to retention settings\n- Should increase as data cycles through retention period\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_reloads_total`**\n- Block reloads triggered (typically 1 per minute)\n- Increases after each compaction cycle\n\n**`prometheus_tsdb_reloads_failures_total`**\n- Failed block reload attempts\n- Alert if: Increases; indicates compacted blocks cannot be loaded\n\n### Distinguishing Healthy vs. Stuck Compaction\n\n**Healthy Compaction Pattern**:\n```\n1. prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total increments\n2. prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block \u2192 1 (for <2 minutes)\n3. prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds records value (1-300s typical)\n4. prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block \u2192 0\n5. prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded momentarily increases, then stabilizes\n6. Repeat every 5-15 minutes during write load\n```\n\n**Stuck Compaction Pattern**:\n```\n1. prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block = 1 (for >10 minutes)\n2. prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds histogram stops recording\n3. prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded increasing or high volatility\n4. prometheus_tsdb_reloads_failures_total increments\n5. Prometheus memory/CPU usage elevated\n6. No new compactions_total increments\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Failure Modes\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Disk Space Exhaustion\n\n**Symptoms**:\n- Compaction progress halts; `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block` stuck at 1\n- Error logs: \"no space left on device\" or \"ENOSPC\"\n- New blocks fail to be created (`.tmp-for-creation` directory cannot be written)\n- Prometheus memory grows as head block accumulates uncompacted data\n- Query latency increases\n\n**Likely Causes**:\n- Retention policy not aggressive enough for ingestion rate\n- Unexpected spike in sample ingestion\n- Compacted blocks not properly cleaned up (parents not deleted)\n- `.tmp-for-deletion` or `.tmp-for-creation` directories persist from crashed compaction\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check available disk space:\n   ```bash\n   df -h /path/to/prometheus/data\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/*\n   ```\n\n2. Identify largest blocks:\n   ```bash\n   cd /path/to/prometheus/data && du -sh */ | sort -rh | head -10\n   ```\n\n3. Check for orphaned temporary directories:\n   ```bash\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data | grep \"tmp-\"\n   ```\n\n4. Examine Prometheus logs for recent compaction attempts:\n   ```bash\n   grep -E \"(compaction|failed)\" /path/to/prometheus.log\n   ```\n\n5. List blocks and check metadata using promtool:\n   ```bash\n   promtool tsdb list /path/to/prometheus/data\n   ```\n\n**Recovery Procedure**:\n\n1. **Increase disk space immediately** (add more storage to the mounted filesystem)\n\n2. **Clean up orphaned temporary directories**:\n   ```bash\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/*.tmp-for-creation\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/*.tmp-for-deletion\n   ```\n\n3. **Delete old blocks exceeding retention** (if aggressive cleanup is safe):\n   ```bash\n   # Identify minimum block time to keep (e.g., 7 days ago in milliseconds)\n   MIN_TIME=$(($(date +%s) - 7*24*3600))000\n\n   for blockdir in /path/to/prometheus/data/*/; do\n     ULID=$(basename \"$blockdir\")\n     # Extract timestamp from ULID (first 10 characters = timestamp in 10ms units)\n     BLOCKTIME=$((16#${ULID:0:8} * 1000))\n     if [ $BLOCKTIME -lt $MIN_TIME ]; then\n       rm -rf \"$blockdir\"\n     fi\n   done\n   ```\n\n4. **Trigger compaction manually** (if Prometheus is still running):\n   ```bash\n   # Use Prometheus HTTP API if available\n   curl -X POST http://localhost:9090/-/clean-tombstones\n   ```\n\n5. **If necessary, stop Prometheus and compact externally**:\n   ```bash\n   # Stop Prometheus\n   systemctl stop prometheus\n\n   # Wait for graceful shutdown (~30s)\n\n   # Trigger manual compaction (if Prometheus has built-in CLI support)\n   # Or restart to allow normal compaction\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   ```\n\n6. **Monitor recovery**:\n   ```bash\n   # Watch disk usage decrease\n   watch -n 5 \"du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data\"\n\n   # Monitor compaction metric\n   curl http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total\n   ```\n\n7. **Adjust retention policy** to prevent recurrence:\n   ```yaml\n   # In prometheus.yml\n   global:\n     retention: \"15d\"      # or reduce if disk-constrained\n     retention_size: \"50GB\"  # hard limit on storage\n   ```\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 2: Compaction Stuck / Not Progressing\n\n**Symptoms**:\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block = 1` for extended period (>10 minutes)\n- No new `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` increments\n- Head blocks accumulating without being persisted\n- Prometheus memory usage climbing (uncompacted head data)\n- Query latency degrading over time\n\n**Likely Causes**:\n- Deadlock in compaction mutex (`cmtx`) due to concurrent compaction and query\n- Hung I/O operation (slow disk, NFS timeout, filesystem fsck)\n- Out-of-memory condition killing compaction goroutine\n- Context cancellation not properly handled\n- Corrupted block preventing reload (blocks loading after compaction fails)\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check if Prometheus is responsive to queries:\n   ```bash\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=up | head -20\n   ```\n\n2. Monitor current goroutines and memory:\n   ```bash\n   # Check process status\n   ps aux | grep prometheus\n\n   # Check memory/CPU\n   top -p <prometheus-pid>\n\n   # Get goroutine count and memory via pprof\n   curl http://localhost:6060/debug/pprof/goroutine | grep \"goroutine\"\n   curl http://localhost:6060/debug/pprof/heap | grep \"alloc_space\"\n   ```\n\n3. Check filesystem I/O:\n   ```bash\n   # Monitor I/O on Prometheus data directory\n   iotop -o -k -p <prometheus-pid>\n\n   # Check for stuck I/O operations\n   lsof -p <prometheus-pid> | grep prometheus/data\n   ```\n\n4. Examine Prometheus logs for context cancellation or blocked goroutines:\n   ```bash\n   tail -f /path/to/prometheus.log | grep -i -E \"(compact|context|cancel|deadline)\"\n   ```\n\n5. Use pprof to capture goroutine dump:\n   ```bash\n   curl http://localhost:6060/debug/pprof/goroutine?debug=2 > /tmp/goroutine.txt\n   grep -A 20 \"compactBlocks\\|compactHead\\|Compact\" /tmp/goroutine.txt\n   ```\n\n**Recovery Procedure**:\n\n1. **Try graceful shutdown first** (signals may unblock I/O):\n   ```bash\n   systemctl stop prometheus\n   # Wait up to 120 seconds for shutdown\n   sleep 120\n   ```\n\n2. **If Prometheus is hung**, use kill signal:\n   ```bash\n   # SIGTERM (graceful)\n   kill -TERM <prometheus-pid>\n   sleep 30\n\n   # SIGKILL (forced) if SIGTERM doesn't work\n   kill -9 <prometheus-pid>\n   ```\n\n3. **Restart Prometheus**:\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   ```\n\n4. **Monitor compaction after restart**:\n   ```bash\n   # Watch for compaction progress\n   watch -n 2 \"curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total | grep -o '\\\"value\\\":\\[[^]]*' | tail -1\"\n\n   # Monitor memory growth\n   watch -n 5 \"ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep\"\n   ```\n\n5. **If compaction still stuck after restart**:\n   - Check for corrupted blocks (see Failure Mode 3)\n   - Manually remove recently compacted blocks if they cannot be loaded:\n     ```bash\n     systemctl stop prometheus\n     # Remove blocks created in last 1 hour\n     find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \"meta.json\" -mmin -60 -print0 | xargs -0 dirname | xargs rm -rf\n     systemctl start prometheus\n     ```\n\n6. **Check for OOM condition** (see Failure Mode 4):\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | grep -E \"(Killed|OOM|memory)\" | tail -20\n   ```\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Block Corruption\n\n**Symptoms**:\n- Errors in logs: \"block corrupted\", \"invalid block\", \"index corrupted\", \"chunk corruption detected\"\n- `prometheus_tsdb_reloads_failures_total` increments\n- Queries return errors or unexpected results from specific time ranges\n- Compaction cannot proceed because corrupted block cannot be loaded\n- Block appears in `promtool list` but `promtool analyze` fails\n\n**Likely Causes**:\n- Partial write during compaction (unclean shutdown, process killed mid-write)\n- Disk corruption (bad sectors, filesystem inconsistency)\n- Memory corruption during compaction (rare, but possible with faulty RAM)\n- Index or chunk file truncated or partially overwritten\n- Incompatible Prometheus version writing block that current version cannot read\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Identify corrupted block from logs:\n   ```bash\n   grep -i \"corrupted\\|invalid\" /path/to/prometheus.log | head -5\n   # Look for ULID in error message\n   ```\n\n2. Verify block integrity with promtool:\n   ```bash\n   promtool tsdb list /path/to/prometheus/data\n   # Note which block has issues\n\n   promtool tsdb analyze /path/to/prometheus/data <BLOCK_ULID>\n   ```\n\n3. Check block files directly:\n   ```bash\n   BLOCK_DIR=\"/path/to/prometheus/data/<BLOCK_ULID>\"\n\n   # Verify files exist\n   ls -la \"$BLOCK_DIR\"\n\n   # Check file sizes\n   stat \"$BLOCK_DIR\"/meta.json\n   stat \"$BLOCK_DIR\"/chunks/\n   stat \"$BLOCK_DIR\"/index\n\n   # Check for truncated files (size 0 or much smaller than expected)\n   ```\n\n4. Attempt to dump block contents:\n   ```bash\n   promtool tsdb dump /path/to/prometheus/data --min-time <START> --max-time <END> > /tmp/dump.txt 2>&1\n   # If dump fails for specific time range, that's where corruption is\n   ```\n\n**Recovery Procedure**:\n\n1. **Stop Prometheus immediately** to prevent further corruption:\n   ```bash\n   systemctl stop prometheus\n   ```\n\n2. **Backup corrupted block before deletion** (for debugging):\n   ```bash\n   cp -r /path/to/prometheus/data/<BLOCK_ULID> /path/to/prometheus/data/<BLOCK_ULID>.backup\n   ```\n\n3. **Delete corrupted block**:\n   ```bash\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/<BLOCK_ULID>\n   ```\n\n4. **Clean up associated temporary directories**:\n   ```bash\n   # If block was being compacted when corruption occurred\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/${BLOCK_ULID}.tmp-for-creation\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/${BLOCK_ULID}.tmp-for-deletion\n   ```\n\n5. **If the corrupted block is a compacted block** (contains parent blocks), delete its parents too:\n   ```bash\n   # Extract metadata to find parent ULIDs\n   cat /path/to/prometheus/data/<BLOCK_ULID>.backup/meta.json | jq '.compaction.parents[] | .ulid'\n\n   # Delete each parent\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/<PARENT_ULID>\n   ```\n\n6. **Check and repair filesystem** (if disk corruption suspected):\n   ```bash\n   # Unmount filesystem safely\n   # This requires stopping all services using the mount\n   umount /path/to/prometheus\n\n   # Run filesystem check\n   fsck -n /dev/sdX  # -n for read-only check first\n   fsck -y /dev/sdX  # -y to auto-repair if confident\n\n   # Remount\n   mount /path/to/prometheus\n   ```\n\n7. **Restart Prometheus**:\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   ```\n\n8. **Verify recovery**:\n   ```bash\n   # Check that blocks can be reloaded\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded\n\n   # Run queries to verify data availability\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(http_requests_total[5m])' | head -10\n   ```\n\n9. **Monitor for re-corruption** and investigate underlying cause:\n   - Run `memtest` on RAM if memory corruption suspected\n   - Check disk health with `smartctl`\n   - Review Prometheus version compatibility\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 4: Out-of-Memory (OOM) During Compaction\n\n**Symptoms**:\n- Prometheus process exits abruptly with status 137 or 139 (killed by kernel)\n- Logs show \"cannot allocate memory\" or \"OOM killer invoked\"\n- `dmesg` contains \"Killed\" messages for prometheus process\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds` never records (process dies mid-compaction)\n- System memory usage spikes to 100% before crash\n- Occurs during specific compaction operations (particularly large blocks)\n\n**Likely Causes**:\n- Insufficient memory for compactor to hold open blocks + merge state\n- Accumulation of many small blocks requiring simultaneous loading\n- Chunk pool exhaustion (chunks not being released properly)\n- Large cardinality spike ingesting many new series\n- Compaction of out-of-order (OOO) blocks requiring extra memory\n- Memory leak in compaction code (rare)\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check available memory before crash:\n   ```bash\n   # Monitor memory during compaction\n   watch -n 1 \"free -h; ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep\"\n   ```\n\n2. Check dmesg for OOM killer invocations:\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | grep -i \"oom\\|killed\" | tail -20\n   ```\n\n3. Check Prometheus memory configuration:\n   ```bash\n   ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep\n   # Note ulimit settings\n\n   cat /proc/<prometheus-pid>/limits | grep \"memory\"\n   ```\n\n4. Estimate memory needed for compaction:\n   ```bash\n   # Get block directory sizes\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/*/\n\n   # Typical rule: need (source_block_size * 2) to 3x for merge buffers\n   # Plus heap overhead\n   ```\n\n5. Check for chunk pool exhaustion:\n   ```bash\n   # Look for warnings about chunk pool in logs\n   grep -i \"chunk pool\\|memory\\|alloc\" /path/to/prometheus.log | tail -20\n   ```\n\n**Recovery Procedure**:\n\n1. **Stop Prometheus**:\n   ```bash\n   systemctl stop prometheus\n   ```\n\n2. **Increase available memory** (choose one approach):\n\n   **Option A: Increase system memory** (preferred)\n   - Add RAM to server\n   - May require reboot\n\n   **Option B: Increase swap space** (temporary)\n   ```bash\n   # Create swap file\n   fallocate -l 4G /swapfile\n   chmod 600 /swapfile\n   mkswap /swapfile\n   swapon /swapfile\n\n   # Make permanent\n   echo '/swapfile none swap sw 0 0' >> /etc/fstab\n   ```\n\n   **Option C: Increase JVM/process memory limits**\n   ```bash\n   # Edit systemd service\n   systemctl edit prometheus\n\n   # Add to [Service] section:\n   # MemoryMax=16G\n   # MemoryHigh=14G\n   ```\n\n3. **Reduce write volume** to compaction (reduce retention or increase block duration):\n   ```yaml\n   global:\n     retention: \"7d\"  # Shorter retention = smaller blocks\n\n   # Or increase block duration (restart required)\n   storage:\n     tsdb:\n       max_block_duration: 3h  # Default 2h, increase to reduce block count\n   ```\n\n4. **Manually clean tombstones** to reduce block count:\n   ```bash\n   # Stop Prometheus\n   systemctl stop prometheus\n\n   # This would normally reduce number of blocks via compaction\n   # But we can avoid heavy compaction by manual cleanup\n\n   # Restart\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   ```\n\n5. **Restart Prometheus**:\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   ```\n\n6. **Monitor memory during compaction**:\n   ```bash\n   # In one terminal\n   watch -n 1 \"free -h\"\n\n   # In another terminal\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block\n   ```\n\n7. **If OOM recurs**, reduce ingestion rate:\n   ```yaml\n   # In scrape configs, reduce frequency\n   scrape_interval: 30s  # Default is 15s\n\n   # Or drop high-cardinality metrics\n   metric_relabel_configs:\n     - source_labels: [__name__]\n       regex: 'high_cardinality_metric_.*'\n       action: drop\n   ```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Recovery Procedures Summary Table\n\n| Failure Mode | Primary Symptom | Quick Diagnosis | Immediate Action | Full Recovery |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Disk Full | ENOSPC errors | `df -h /path/to/prometheus/data` | Add storage OR delete temp dirs | Clean old blocks, adjust retention |\n| Stuck Compaction | `compaction_populating_block=1` for >10min | `curl prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` | Restart Prometheus | Check for I/O hangs, corrupted blocks |\n| Block Corruption | \"invalid block\" in logs | `promtool tsdb analyze` | Stop Prometheus, delete block | Rebuild from backup, check filesystem |\n| OOM Killer | Process exits 137, dmesg OOM | `free -h; dmesg \\| grep -i oom` | Add swap OR restart | Increase memory, reduce retention |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code References\n\n### Critical Functions by Failure Mode\n\n**Compaction Triggering & Planning** (`tsdb/compact.go`):\n- `LeveledCompactor.Plan()` at lines 222-240: Identifies which blocks to compact\n- `LeveledCompactor.plan()` at lines 242-338: Internal planning logic, checks for overlaps and failures\n- `LeveledCompactor.selectDirs()` at lines 342-380: Selects non-overlapping blocks for Operational Best Practices\n\n### Proactive Monitoring Setup\n\n1. **Alert on compaction stall**:\n   ```yaml\n   - alert: TsdbCompactionNotProgressing\n     expr: rate(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total[5m]) == 0\n     for: 10m\n     annotations:\n       summary: \"Prometheus compaction not progressing\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Alert on excessive OOM compactions**:\n   ```yaml\n   - alert: TsdbCompactionOOM\n     expr: increase(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_oom_errors_total[5m]) > 0\n     annotations:\n       summary: \"Compaction OOM errors detected\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Alert on block reload failures**:\n   ```yaml\n   - alert: TsdbReloadsFailed\n     expr: rate(prometheus_tsdb_reloads_failures_total[5m]) > 0\n     annotations:\n       summary: \"TSDB block reload failures\"\n   ```\n\n### Maintenance Windows\n\n- **Monthly block integrity check**:\n  ```bash\n  promtool tsdb list /path/to/prometheus/data\n  promtool tsdb analyze /path/to/prometheus/data <recent_block_ulid>\n  ```\n\n- **Quarterly retention audit**:\n  - Review disk usage vs. retention policy\n  - Adjust block duration if high memory usage during compaction\n  - Verify oldest blocks are being properly deleted\n\n### Retention Policy Tuning\n\nUse this formula to set retention:\n```\nretention_size \u2248 (average_ingestion_rate_Mbps) \u00d7 (retention_days) \u00d7 86400 \u00d7 1.2\n```\n\nExample: 10 Mbps ingestion, 15-day retention:\n```\n10 \u00d7 15 \u00d7 86400 \u00d7 1.2 \u2248 15.5 GB storage needed\n```\n\nConfigure in Prometheus:\n```yaml\nglobal:\n  retention: \"15d\"\n  retention_size: \"16GB\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. # Prometheus TSDB Compaction Operational Runbook

## 1. Overview

### Purpose of Compaction

TSDB (Time Series Database) compaction in Prometheus serves three critical functions:

1. **Block Consolidation**: Merges overlapping time blocks to reduce the number of files that need to be queried
2. **Tombstone Cleanup**: Physically removes series marked for deletion by applying tombstone metadata, reducing disk footprint
3. **Query Performance**: Maintains optimal query performance by keeping block sizes and levels balanced according to exponential growth

Without compaction, Prometheus would accumulate small blocks indefinitely, degrading query performance and consuming excessive disk space. Compaction is triggered automatically by Prometheus and typically requires no manual intervention.

### Block Structure and Compaction Levels

**Block Basics**:
- Each block represents a time-ordered chunk of time series data
- Blocks have half-open time intervals: `[MinTime, MaxTime)` where MaxTime is exclusive
- Block structure includes: chunks (samples), index (series metadata), tombstones (deletion markers), meta.json (metadata)
- Block identifiers are ULIDs (Universally Unique Lexicographically Sortable Identifiers)

**Compaction Levels**:
Prometheus uses exponential block ranges to organize blocks hierarchically. Given default configuration:
- **Level 0** (Head blocks): ~2 hours of data from active writes
- **Level 1**: Result of compacting Level 0 blocks (~6 hours = 3 × 2h)
- **Level 2**: Result of compacting Level 1 blocks (~18 hours = 3 × 6h)
- **Level 3+**: Continue exponential growth with factor of 3

This is configured via `DefaultBlockDuration` (2 hours) and exponential step factor (3) in `tsdb/db.go:745-749`.

**Block Metadata Tracking**:
Each compacted block includes:
- 
... (truncated)
